    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2186304844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2186304844" />
    <a title="Scot Eaton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7429632-scot-eaton"><img alt="Scot Eaton" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2186304844?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scot Eaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scot Eaton" href="/user/show/7429632-scot-eaton">Scot Eaton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2186304844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1061356067002109102">I feel that "classic" works of any medium should be divided into 2 categories:<br/>1. Classics of the Art - works that appeal to people who participate in the craft. They push the boundaries of what the craft was originally thought to do.<br/>2. Classics of the Heart - works that have a timeless quality to them, that can be enjoyed apart from any historical context.<br/><br/>So when I heard that "The Book of the New Sun" was a Sci-Fi/Fantasy (SFF) classic, like "The Lord of the Rings", I assumed that like LotR, it </span>
  <span id="freeText1061356067002109102" style="display:none">I feel that "classic" works of any medium should be divided into 2 categories:<br />1. Classics of the Art - works that appeal to people who participate in the craft. They push the boundaries of what the craft was originally thought to do.<br />2. Classics of the Heart - works that have a timeless quality to them, that can be enjoyed apart from any historical context.<br /><br />So when I heard that "The Book of the New Sun" was a Sci-Fi/Fantasy (SFF) classic, like "The Lord of the Rings", I assumed that like LotR, it was a Classic of the Heart. Most of my disappointment from this book has to do with the expectation I went in with. The Book of the New Sun is very firmly a Classic of the Art. It appeals to people who are invested in literature, and for those who are invested in the craft of SFF. However, it will hold little appeal if you are not in either of those camps.<br /><br />I've heard it said multiple times on Goodreads that Gene Wolfe needs to be read a minimum of twice. Having read the New Sun quartet, I can see that. The book seems VERY arbitrary and random the first time you read it; the main character seems to wander through his own story with no apparent goal or purpose. Everything has an explanation, and everything wraps up in the end. EDIT: I have now read "The Urth of the New Sun", and I can no longer refer to this as a quartet. It is a quintet, and you must read all 5. Book 4 stops the story, but it does not end the story. Book 5 ties all of the loose, disparate pieces together for a true conclusion.<br /><br />So what makes this book unique? What makes it a Classic of the Art? First off, it is a cross between a SFF story and a philosophy text. It is told in first person with an imperfect narrator. As Severian recounts the events of his life, he will often wander into tangents as to the deeper meaning of things. Many of these wanderings are truly thought-provoking, and would appeal to literature buffs and people who want to explore the true literary merit of SFF. Second, it is a story of Earth (or Urth) millions of years in the future, with a dying sun, and in a period of Dark Ages, but it never explains explicitly how the world got there. It throws out tidbits of its history (the moon is Green, so it was obviously terraformed at some point; humanity went to the stars also), but is written from the perspective of someone who just accepts things as they are. Third, it has very interesting ideas. A sword with a mercury core that enhances the strength of the swinger? Pretty cool. Fuligin, a color darker than black that is so black it makes things seem 2D? Neat, and also real now that Vantablack exists. In my time reading this book, these unique points made me never regret having picked up the book.<br /><br />So what makes this book NOT a Classic of the Heart? Simply put, it is hard to follow the story. Book 1 ends with jarring abruptness, and Book 2 picks up some time later without explaining what happened in between. Book 5 begins with a 100-page semi-psychedelic stream of consciousness. Even the events that lead to Severian becoming Autarch (not a spoiler, he tells you in the beginning of the book that he is writing as the Autarch) seem like a random string of events that were set up only 1-2 chapers prior. There is a pivotal scene in Book 2 (regarding a creature known as the Alzabo), that the reader won't understand for hundreds of more pages. Worse though is that Severian isn't a likeable character. There's no redemption ark, because he never sees his employment as a torturer as a thing that is wrong. He has sex with almost every woman in the story, sometimes minutes after meeting them. Until the last half of book 5, I never rooted for him; I never wanted him to win; I never cared what would happen next. That's a cardinal sin for a story of this length told through a first-person perspective.<br /><br />So I'm firmly middle of the road on this series. Gene Wolfe is excellent at the craft of writing, and I can understand WHY this book is a Classic of the Art. However, I just didn't care enough about the story or the characters, and I don't see any places for a casual reader to get attached to them either. I give this book 3 stars. Some people will love it, and some will not.<br />EDIT: After reading "The Urth of the New Sun", I'm bumping this up to a 3.5. It was the ending the book needed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1061356067002109102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2112324514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2112324514" />
    <a title="Grace Harwood" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16438199-grace-harwood"><img alt="Grace Harwood" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442658079p2/16438199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2112324514?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace Harwood" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace Harwood" href="/user/show/16438199-grace-harwood">Grace Harwood</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2112324514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18376748875573863444">In a time before Game of Thrones (did such a time ever exist?) I never read fantasy or sci-fi novels. That time has now passed and this novel - if you are GOT fan - is simply awesome. In fact, there's a lot in here that is awfully reminiscent of GOT (or rather, GOT is reminiscent of this, being as this predates GOT).<br/><br/>The story is as follows: Severian, a young, very large, man is a member of the sinister guild of torturers. However, he is disgraced when he falls in love with one of the 'clients' a</span>
  <span id="freeText18376748875573863444" style="display:none">In a time before Game of Thrones (did such a time ever exist?) I never read fantasy or sci-fi novels. That time has now passed and this novel - if you are GOT fan - is simply awesome. In fact, there's a lot in here that is awfully reminiscent of GOT (or rather, GOT is reminiscent of this, being as this predates GOT).<br /><br />The story is as follows: Severian, a young, very large, man is a member of the sinister guild of torturers. However, he is disgraced when he falls in love with one of the 'clients' and provides her with the means to free herself from the tortures she must endure. As a result of this, he is exiled from his guild and sent off to take up a new placement in the distant city of Thrax. All he has to take with him is his guild cloak (which covers him like a shadow, hence the first book in this collection being called 'The Shadow of the Torturer' and an ancient sword called 'Terminus Est'. The story then follows his adventures as he travels to his new assignment. <br /><br />There is so much that is wonderful about this book. The characters are fabulously realised. Severian himself is a multi-faceted hero with all the strength of the torturer, but a surprising depth of humanity and empathy despite the nature of his 'work'. By turns warm and romantic and also cold, harsh and unforgiving, Severian is a hero whose surprising adventures you won't want to leave, despite his many appeals to the reader 'to walk no farther with me reader, [...] it is no easy road.' (These direct appeals to the reader was something else I very much enjoyed about it).<br /><br />The heroines he happens across (and Severian falls in love with nearly all of them, suffering no doubt, with his romantic nature) are equally sublime. This is also a book with a message about the society we live in, taking place in a post-historic Earth where 'all men are torturers, one way or another' in the wrongs they have inflicted upon society. It is a pointed commentary upon the feudal nature of a society which doesn't take women's views into account. It is also a statement about the constructed nature of masculinity - Severian's manly nature suffers everytime he loses Terminus Est.<br /><br />In short, I loved this book. The first one was definitely the best. I felt the Claw of the Conciliator (the second book) was a bit more bitty and lost the plot a little, but it's worth persevering to the end. This is an awesome story to fill that Game of Thrones vacancy we all have to endure as we while away the time until Season 8.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18376748875573863444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EC7AMBX0YtmUOiQ0ZdWCvkMZirvE2yQIbRtN22U6QO7w/5WLZR7DMkETaCocTWo512qvA10JZERPEkSUjsH1PA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

The attack is part of a Tyranni plot to eliminate all resistance leaders, one of whom had been his own father. Now Biron has been chosen to step into his father\'s shoes and rally the rebellion. But once he casts his lot with the freedom fighters, he will find himself guarding against treachery on every side and facing the most difficult choice of his young life: to betray either the woman he loves or the revolution his father died to protect.\nThe Currents of Space: Thousands of years after the events of The Stars, Like Dust, a man named Rik is wiped of his mind and deposited on the planet Florina-a wimpering, thumb-sucking half-child. Valona, a lonely peasant girl, adopts and takes care of him, and slowly his memory returns. But what he remembers entangles the pair in a web of interplanetary intrigue, in which they\'re hunted by high-ranking officials and spies.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/23069.Gene_Wolfe">About Gene Wolfe</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/23069.Gene_Wolfe"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1556979018p3/23069.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/23069.Gene_Wolfe">Gene Wolfe
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7585499929129639405">Gene Wolfe was an American science fiction and fantasy writer. He was noted for his dense, allusive prose as well as the strong influence of his Catholic faith, to which he converted after marrying a Catholic. He was a prolific short story writer and a novelist, and has won many awards in the field.<br/><br/>The Damon Knight Memorial Grand Master Award is given by SFWA for ‘lifetime achievement in science f</span>
  <span id="freeText7585499929129639405" style="display:none">Gene Wolfe was an American science fiction and fantasy writer. He was noted for his dense, allusive prose as well as the strong influence of his Catholic faith, to which he converted after marrying a Catholic. He was a prolific short story writer and a novelist, and has won many awards in the field.<br /><br />The Damon Knight Memorial Grand Master Award is given by SFWA for ‘lifetime achievement in science fiction and/or fantasy.’ Wolfe joins the Grand Master ranks alongside such legends as Connie Willis, Michael Moorcock, Anne McCaffrey, Robert Silverberg, Ursula K. Le Guin, Isaac Asimov, Ray Bradbury and Joe Haldeman. The award will be presented at the 48th Annual Nebula Awards Weekend in San Jose, CA, May 16-19, 2013.<br /><br />While attending Texas A&amp;M University Wolfe published his first speculative fiction in The Commentator, a student literary journal. Wolfe dropped out during his junior year, and was drafted to fight in the Korean War. After returning to the United States he earned a degree from the University of Houston and became an industrial engineer. He edited the journal Plant Engineering for many years before retiring to write full-time, but his most famous professional engineering achievement is a contribution to the machine used to make Pringles potato crisps. He lived in Barrington, Illinois, a suburb of Chicago.<br /><br />A frequent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/award/show/9-hugo-award" rel="nofollow noopener">Hugo</a> nominee without a win, Wolfe has nevertheless picked up several <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/award/show/23-nebula-award" rel="nofollow noopener">Nebula</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/award/show/46-locus-award" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus</a> Awards, among others, including the World Fantasy Award for Life Achievement and the 2012 Damon Knight Memorial Grand Master Award. He is also a member of the Science Fiction Hall of Fame.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/genewolfe">http://us.macmillan.com/author/genewolfe</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7585499929129639405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

  <!--
This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
